# Analysis of Ground Truth

Let me first expand the GT expression:

$$GT = 31.12 \cdot \epsilon \cdot (-0.05295(T - 316.19) + 1) - 0.2255(T - 316.19) + 3.629 \cdot \epsilon^{0.5976}(T - 316.19)$$

Expanding:
$$GT = 31.12\epsilon \cdot (-0.05295T + 16.74 + 1) - 0.2255T + 71.31 + 3.629\epsilon^{0.5976}T - 3.629 \cdot 316.19 \cdot \epsilon^{0.5976}$$

$$= -1.648 \cdot T \cdot \epsilon + 31.12 \cdot 17.74 \cdot \epsilon - 0.2255T + 71.31 + 3.629T\epsilon^{0.5976} - 1147.1\epsilon^{0.5976}$$

Wait, let me be more careful. Let me denote $c_2 = c_5 = c_8 = 316.19$.

$$GT = c_0\epsilon(-c_1(T-c_2) + c_3) - c_4(T-c_2) + \epsilon^{c_6} \cdot c_7(T-c_2)$$

Expanding:
$$= -c_0 c_1 \epsilon T + c_0 c_1 c_2 \epsilon + c_0 c_3 \epsilon - c_4 T + c_4 c_2 + c_7 T \epsilon^{c_6} - c_7 c_2 \epsilon^{c_6}$$

So the GT has these basis function terms:
1. $T \cdot \epsilon$ (coefficient: $-c_0 c_1 = -31.12 \times 0.05295 = -1.648$)
2. $\epsilon$ (coefficient: $c_0 c_1 c_2 + c_0 c_3 = 31.12 \times 0.05295 \times 316.19 + 31.12 = 552.0 + 31.12 = 552.0 + 31.12 ≈ 552.1$) Wait let me recalculate: $31.12 \times 0.05295 \times 316.19 = 31.12 \times 16.74 = 520.9 + 31.12 = 552.0$
3. $T$ (coefficient: $-c_4 + c_7 \cdot 0 = -0.2255$) Wait, $-c_4 = -0.2255$
4. constant (coefficient: $c_4 c_2 = 0.2255 \times 316.19 = 71.30$)
5. $T \cdot \epsilon^{c_6}$ (coefficient: $c_7 = 3.629$)
6. $\epsilon^{c_6}$ (coefficient: $-c_7 c_2 = -3.629 \times 316.19 = -1147.1$)

So GT = $a_1 T\epsilon + a_2 \epsilon + a_3 T + a_4 + a_5 T\epsilon^{0.5976} + a_6 \epsilon^{0.5976}$

The key basis functions are: $T\epsilon$, $\epsilon$, $T$, $1$, $T\epsilon^{c_6}$, $\epsilon^{c_6}$

Note that $T\epsilon^{c_6}$ is a critical term - it couples $T$ with a fractional power of $\epsilon$.

## GT Analysis

The GT expression is:
```
c0*epsilon*(-c1*(T - c2) + c3) - c4*(T - c5) + epsilon**c6*c7*(T - c8)
```

With c2 = c5 = c8 = 316.1945..., let me denote this common value as K.

Expanding:
```
c0*epsilon*(-c1*T + c1*K + c3) - c4*T + c4*K + c7*epsilon**c6*T - c7*epsilon**c6*K
```

Grouping by terms:
- **T terms**: -c0*c1*epsilon*T - c4*T + c7*epsilon**c6*T = T*(-c0*c1*epsilon - c4 + c7*epsilon**c6)
- **Constant terms** (no T): c0*epsilon*(c1*K + c3) + c4*K - c7*K*epsilon**c6
  = c0*(c1*K + c3)*epsilon + c4*K - c7*K*epsilon**c6

So the GT has the structure:
```
T*(-c4) + T*(-c0*c1)*epsilon + T*c7*epsilon**c6 + c0*(c1*K+c3)*epsilon + c4*K - c7*K*epsilon**c6
```

This gives us basis functions in terms of T and epsilon:
1. **T** (linear in T, no epsilon)
2. **T*epsilon** (linear in both T and epsilon)
3. **T*epsilon^c6** (T times fractional power of epsilon, c6 ≈ 0.598)
4. **epsilon** (just epsilon)
5. **constant** (just a number)
6. **epsilon^c6** (fractional power of epsilon)

The key distinguishing feature is the **T*epsilon^c6** term. This is critical - any matching candidate must be able to produce this term.

Let me now check each candidate for the ability to generate all 6 basis functions, especially T*epsilon^c6.

### Candidates 1-12, 17-20: Polynomial-type candidates

These candidates have terms like T*c0, T*c1*epsilon, epsilon**c_i, epsilon**2, epsilon, constants. None of them have a **T*epsilon^c** term (T multiplied by a fractional power of epsilon).

Let me check if any can produce T*epsilon^c6:

**Candidate 1**: T*c0 + T*c1*epsilon + c2*epsilon**c3 + c4*epsilon**2 + c5*epsilon + c6*epsilon**c7
- Has T, T*epsilon, epsilon**c3, epsilon**2, epsilon, epsilon**c7. No T*epsilon^c term. **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 2**: T*c0*epsilon + c1 + c2*epsilon**c3 + c4*epsilon**2 + c5*epsilon + c6*epsilon**c7
- Has T*epsilon, constant, epsilon**c3, epsilon**2, epsilon, epsilon**c7. Missing T alone and T*epsilon^c. Can set c0's coefficient but still missing T*epsilon^c. **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 3**: Everything divided by (c1*epsilon + c2). Let me multiply through:
```
[T*c0 + T*c3*epsilon + c4*epsilon**c5 + c6*epsilon**2 + c7*epsilon + c8*epsilon*epsilon**c5 + c9] / (c1*epsilon + c2)
```
Numerator: T*c0 + T*c3*epsilon + c4*epsilon**c5 + c6*epsilon**2 + c7*epsilon + c8*epsilon^(1+c5) + c9

For this to equal GT*(c1*epsilon + c2), I need to expand GT*(c1*epsilon + c2) and match. This gets complicated. The GT has T*epsilon^c6 which when multiplied by (c1*epsilon + c2) gives c2*T*epsilon^c6 + c1*T*epsilon^(1+c6). The numerator has T*c0 and T*c3*epsilon but no T*epsilon^c6 term. So **NO MATCH**.

**Candidate 4**: T*c0 + T*c1*epsilon + c2 + c3*epsilon**c4 + c5*epsilon**2 + c6*epsilon + c7*epsilon**c8 + c9*epsilon
- Same as Candidate 1 with extra constant and epsilon terms. No T*epsilon^c. **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 5**: T*c0 + T*c1*epsilon + T*c2 + c3 + c4*epsilon**c5 + c6*epsilon**2 + c7*epsilon + c8*epsilon**c9
- T*(c0+c2) + T*c1*epsilon + ... No T*epsilon^c. **NO MATCH**

**Candidates 6-12, 17-20**: Similar structure - T, T*epsilon, powers of epsilon, constants. None have T*epsilon^c. **ALL NO MATCH**

### Candidates 13-14, 21, 34: Log/exp candidates without T*epsilon^c
These use log and exp of epsilon but not T*epsilon^c. **NO MATCH**

### Candidate 15: T**c0*c1 + ... 
Has T^c0 instead of T. If c0=1, this gives T*c1, but no T*epsilon term. Missing T*epsilon and T*epsilon^c. **NO MATCH**

### Candidate 16: T*c0 + c1*epsilon**c2 + c3 + c4*epsilon**c5 + c6*epsilon**2
Missing T*epsilon and T*epsilon^c. **NO MATCH**

### Candidates 22-50: More complex candidates

For any candidate to match, it must produce the term **T*epsilon^c6** (with c6 ≈ 0.598). Let me scan for candidates that can produce this.

**Candidate 24**: T*c0/(c1+epsilon) = T*c0*sum of powers via expansion? No, this is T/(c1+epsilon) which is a rational function of epsilon, not T*epsilon^c.

**Candidate 28**: T*c0/(c1+epsilon) + T*c2 + ... Has T*c2 and T*c0/(c1+epsilon) but no T*epsilon^c.

**Candidate 35**: T*c0 + c1*epsilon**c2 + c3*epsilon**c4 + c5 + c6/(T*c7+c8) + c9*epsilon + sqrt(epsilon**2)
Has 1/T term and |epsilon|. Under domain constraints |epsilon|=epsilon. But has 1/T, no T*epsilon, no T*epsilon^c. Can set c6=0 to kill 1/T term, but then missing T*epsilon and T*epsilon^c. **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 36**: T*c0 + c1*epsilon**c2 + c3*epsilon**c4 + c5*exp(c6*epsilon) + c7 + sqrt(epsilon**2)
No T*epsilon, no T*epsilon^c. **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 42**: T*c0 + T*c1*(c2+epsilon)**c3 + c4*epsilon**c5 + c6 + c7*epsilon/(T*c8+c9) + sqrt(epsilon**2)
This has T*c1*(c2+epsilon)**c3. If c2=0, this becomes T*c1*epsilon**c3, which gives T*epsilon^c! Also has T*c0, epsilon**c5, constant, epsilon/(T*...), |epsilon|=epsilon.

Setting c2=0: T*c0 + T*c1*epsilon**c3 + c4*epsilon**c5 + c6 + c7*epsilon/(T*c8+c9) + epsilon

The c7*epsilon/(T*c8+c9) term: set c7=0 to eliminate it.
Then: T*c0 + T*c1*epsilon**c3 + c4*epsilon**c5 + c6 + epsilon

GT needs: T*A + T*B*epsilon + T*C*epsilon^0.598 + D*epsilon + E + F*epsilon^0.598

We need T*epsilon (T times epsilon^1). Setting c3=1 gives T*c1*epsilon, but then we lose T*epsilon^0.598. Setting c3=0.598 gives T*epsilon^0.598 but loses T*epsilon.

We can't get both T*epsilon AND T*epsilon^c6 from one T*(c2+epsilon)^c3 term. **NO MATCH**

None of the candidates can produce all three: T, T*epsilon, and T*epsilon^c6 simultaneously.

After careful analysis, **no candidate matches**.
